## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor rate laws / ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ordinary differential equation for the time evolution of a chemical species concentration A in a (typically well-mixed) kinetic system. With only t and A available, the most common structures are concentration-dependent rate laws (reaction order, autocatalysis, reversibility) and/or explicitly time-dependent rate coefficients (forcing, deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated catalyst regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (elementary unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order approximation)
- n-th / power-law kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order, including fractional orders)
- Offset (background production/consumption): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net formation plus linear loss; linearized kinetics near an operating point)
- Approach to equilibrium (reversible first-order lumping): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type in concentration): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating reaction with finite limiting concentration)
- Prout–Tompkins-type autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A)**c3 (sigmoidal kinetics with adjustable early/late-time behavior)
- Product/inhibition-modified power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (A**c2 + c3) (rate suppression at high A; e.g., crowding, self-inhibition, transport limitation)
- Substrate inhibition (Haldane-like rational form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A**2 + c1 * A + c2) (rate peaks at intermediate A, then decreases at higher A)
- Time-varying rate coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions over time, e.g., slow temperature ramp or catalyst activation/deactivation trend)
- Catalyst/activity deactivation forcing: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decays in time due to catalyst deactivation or reagent depletion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is always negative and roughly proportional to A, a first-order mechanism is likely; curvature in ln(A) vs t indicates deviations from first order.
- If dA_dt scales with A**n (n>1), consumption accelerates strongly at higher A (bimolecular/chain termination-like behavior); early-time depletion can be slow if A starts small.
- A term of the form -(A - c1) indicates relaxation to a nonzero steady concentration (reversibility or equilibrium constraint), implying A(t) asymptotes to c1.
- Autocatalytic forms A*(c1-A) or A^p*(c1-A)^q imply sigmoidal time courses: slow initiation, rapid middle conversion, then slowdown near completion.
- Rational inhibition forms with A in both numerator and denominator can produce a maximum rate at intermediate A, characteristic of self-inhibition, crowding, or transport limitations at high concentration.
- Explicit t-dependence in the effective rate coefficient (e.g., (c0+c1*t) or exp(-c*t)) suggests non-stationary experimental conditions such as catalyst deactivation, changing light intensity, or feed/temperature programming.
- A constant term in dA_dt (±c0) indicates an external source/sink independent of current A (e.g., constant feed, zero-order surface reaction, or background loss).
- Sign changes in dA_dt as A crosses a level (e.g., proportional to -(A-c1)) indicate a stable fixed point where production and consumption balance.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK4)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,A)= -0.1149290460\,A^2 \;+\; 0.06806555110\,A\cdot \log(0.2569297861\,t+1).
\]
Key structural facts about GT:

- It has exactly two \(A\)-dependences: an \(A^2\) polynomial term and an \(A\cdot \log(\text{affine in }t)\) term.
- The only non-polynomial dependence on \(t\) is \(\log(\alpha t+1)\), multiplied by \(A\).
- There is **no** constant term independent of \(A\), and no plain \(A\) term independent of \(t\).

So any candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by setting some candidate constants to 0 and choosing exponents) to “(constant)\(A^2\) + (constant)\(A\log(\alpha t+\beta)\)”, with no extra \(t\)-functions (powers, roots, rationals, sin, exp, etc.). None of the candidates even contain a \(\log\), so the only way they could match is if their \(t\)-dependent part could *equal* \(\log(\alpha t+1)\) for all \(t\), which is impossible for the function families shown (algebraic powers/roots/rationals/sin/exp).

Now, candidate-by-candidate:

1. \(A c0 + A c1 (c2+t)^{c3} + A^{c4}c5\): only power-law in \(t\), no log. Cannot equal \(A\log(\alpha t+1)\) for all \(t\). No match.

2. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A c2/\sqrt{c3+t} + A c4 (c5+t)^{c6}\): \(t\)-dependence is algebraic (root/power), not log. No match.

3. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A c2 + A c3/\sqrt{c4+t} + A c5 (c6+t)^{c7}\): same issue; no log. No match.

4. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A c2 (c3+t)^{c4} + c5\): has an \(A\cdot\)power term, not \(A\log\). Also has constant \(c5\) unless set 0. Still no log. No match.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK4)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.11493·A² + 0.06807·A·log(0.25693·t + 1)**

The key basis functions in the GT are:
1. **A²** (with a constant coefficient)
2. **A·log(c₃·t + c₄)** — a logarithmic function of t multiplied by A

For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce exactly these two basis functions and no others. Let me analyze the candidates.

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `A·log(linear_in_t)`. None of the candidates contain an explicit `log()` function. So I need to check if any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates (like `1/sqrt(t)`, `(c+t)^c`, `1/(c+t)`, `sqrt(c+t)`, `sin()`, `exp()`) can exactly reproduce `log(c·t + 1)`.

**Can `(c₄ + t)^c₅` equal `log(c·t + 1)`?** No. A power function `(a+t)^b` for any fixed real `b` cannot equal `log(c·t+1)` for all t. These are fundamentally different function classes — power functions vs logarithmic functions. Setting `c₅ → 0` gives a constant, not a log. No value of `c₅` makes a power function into a logarithm.

**Can combinations of `1/sqrt(c+t)`, `1/(c+t)`, `sqrt(c+t)` produce `log(c·t+1)`?** No. These are algebraic functions (power functions with specific exponents), and `log` is transcendental. No finite linear combination of power functions of `(c+t)` can equal `log(c·t+1)`.

**Can `sin()` or `exp()` terms help?** No — `sin` and `exp` are linearly independent from `log`.

Let me verify: every single candidate uses combinations of:
- Polynomial terms in A (A², A)
- `A/sqrt(c+t)` terms
- `A·(c+t)^c` terms  
- `A/(c·t+c)` terms
- `sin()`, `exp()`, `sqrt()` terms
- Constants

None of these can produce `A·log(c·t + 1)`. The logarithmic basis function is **missing** from every candidate.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically: Every candidate contains terms like `(c+t)^c`, `1/sqrt(c+t)`, `1/(c+t)`, `sqrt(c+t)`, `sin()`, `exp()`, or constants — none contain `log()`. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), no combination of power functions can exactly equal a logarithmic function across the entire domain.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
